# 1.1 NUCLEOPHILES AND ELECTROPHILES: THE1.1 NUCLEOPHLES AND ELECTROPHILES:THE $\tt s _ { N } 2$ PARADIGM2PARADIGM

In this book, we will be overwhelmingly concerned with polar or ionic mechanisms. TheseInthis book.we w e overwhelmnglyconcrned wmhpolr or onic mechansms.Ihe involve the movement of electron pairs, unlike radical reactions which involve unpairedolvethe movement ot ecctron pars,uke ndc reactons whch olve unparo electrons. The HSAB conceptoncept of trd and soft Lewis acits and bases-HsA.tor shot.Ihe HSAB concep was introduced by Ralph Pearson over 50 years ago and was subsequently put on a firmerws inroduod bv Ral Person over s0 veas aro and ws sbseauenvput onanme theoretical foundation by Pearson and Parr, among others. Hard acids and bases areeoreucal toundion by Fearson and Fr,amongotes.Hard ais and bses a relatively unpolarizable and have relatively high surface charge density, positive oretveyunpolanzblandhverehtveyhghsutacecargedensiy,postveo negative; soft acids and bases are relatively polarizable and have low surface chargeegave:soft aids and bases ae retvely polnzable and hve ow suace chr density, positive or negative. Of course, there are many borderline cases. High surfacedensty.postve or negave.Ot coure.there re many borderinecses.Hah suao charge density (hardness) typically results from a high formal charge (FC), positive orcare densty(hrdness)prcaly resuts om ahghtoml carre(rC).positveo negative, and small atomic/ionic size, and the opposite is true for low surface charge densityegave,andsmaomcionicse,andthe opposieistre torlowsutacechre densit (softness). The utility of the hardness/softness concept derives from the HSAB principle, whichThe utty of the hrdnesshofess cacept denves tom te HsAE princple.whic states that soft bases react faster and form stronger bonds with soft acids, and hard basessttes tht sot bases react tster nd tom sronger bonds wh sot acids,and hard bse react faster and form stronger bonds with hard acids. # 1.20 RADICAL REACTIONS1.N RAIICALREACIINN

$$

$$

Homolysis refers to the separation of a bonding electron pair into two unpaired electrons,Homolvsis reters tothe senarnon or a bondng eletron nar into tuo unpare electrons that is, radicals. Heterolytic mechanisms, by contrast, are characterized by a bond-breakingats,rndcals.Heterolytcmechnsms bvcontrst,arechrctenzod bYabond-bren step where the electron pair constituting the bond leaves with one of the fragments, as shownepwheretheekcron parconsitutng thebondeaves wthoneofthetrements,asshow below:

$$
\text {H e t e r o l y s i s :} \quad \begin{array}{c c c} A & B & \longrightarrow A ^ {\ominus} + B ^ {\ominus} \\ A & B & \longrightarrow A ^ {\ominus} + B ^ {\ominus} \end{array} \tag {1.73}
$$

# REVIEW PROBLEM 2.3
